“我認為，鑒於宏觀經濟前景，銅價前景仍為負面。”","headline":"金屬期市：倫敦期銅因美元下跌而上漲，市場交投清淡","date":"2015-10-05T08:01:38.857Z","tpc_list":["COM","NCYC","FOBE","FOTB","FOOD1","BMAT","MINE","ENER","MTAL","ALUM","MEMI","COAM","OILG","EXPL","MCE","EMRG","WEU","CH","GB","EUROP","CEEU","CN","ASIA","MKTREP","MIN","REP","CMPNY","LEAD1","TIN1","BASMTL","CPPR","ALU","METL","NKL","ZNC","LZH","RTRS"],"instr_list":["GLEN.L","0#SCF:","0#SAF:","RING=","0#SZN:"]},{"body":"(The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions\r\nexpressed are his own.)    \r\n    \r\n    By Dominic Elliott\r\n    Oct 5 (Reuters Breakingviews) - Poland's short-sighted\r\nenergy policy is making it look more like Brazil than a\r\nfree-market economy that the European Commission expects to grow\r\n3.4 percent next year. The state-controlled supervisory board of\r\nlisted utility Tauron <TPE.WA> last week replaced its boss with\r\na more emollient one to grease the government rescue of the\r\nnation's biggest coal miner.\r\n    The country's coal sector desperately needs restructuring.\r\nThough Poland has Europe's largest reserves - with 14 billion\r\ntonnes of the black stuff, according to Polityka Insight -\r\nstate-controlled mines have lost more than $850 million since\r\nthe start of 2014. Poland has deep mines and thin seams. But\r\nthat fails to account for industry productivity being 77 percent\r\nlower than the average in the largest 15 EU countries, notes\r\nMcKinsey.\r\n    Rather than propping up failing companies, a more radical\r\nrethink is called for: European Commission limits on carbon\r\ndioxide emissions will require Poland to generate less than half\r\nits energy from coal by 2030, down from above 80 percent now.\r\n    With three weeks until the national election, and lagging in\r\nthe polls, the heavy-handedness of Prime Minister Ewa Kopacz\r\nlooks like vote-grabbing. Her incumbent Civic Platform (PO)\r\nparty trails in polls and the coal mining region of Silesia\r\naccounts for a large slice of the electorate. Kopacz previously\r\ntried to face down miners' demands for better wages.\r\n    Poland's otherwise-vibrant economy will suffer from such\r\nintervention. The stock market is already sickly, after pension\r\nreforms swapped equity investments for state IOUs to improve the\r\ncountry's debt profile. Just $400 million was raised through new\r\nstock offerings last year. Though share price moves were limited\r\nfollowing Tauron's board putsch, state interference may be\r\nalready priced in. The government owns more than 50 percent of\r\nthe country's three largest energy companies other than Tauron,\r\nwhere it has 30 percent.\r\n    Privatisation has benefited Poland, in sectors like\r\nfinancial services and even in coal mining - where private\r\ncompany Bogdanka, which is being acquired by utility Enea\r\n<ENAE.WA>, raised productivity by improving capital efficiency\r\nand recruiting from other industries.\r\n    By meddling in mining, Kopacz is following in the fumbling\r\nfootsteps of Brazilian President Dilma Rousseff, who used oil\r\ngiant Petrobras <PETR4.SA> as an instrument of flawed state\r\npolicy. Central planning of this kind was once common under\r\ncommunist rule - Poland shook that off for the better back in\r\n1989.\r\n\r\n    \r\n    <^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^\r\n    SIGN UP FOR BREAKINGVIEWS EMAIL ALERTS:\r\n    www.breakingviews.com/TOPNewsSubscription\r\n    \r\n    ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^>\r\n    \r\n    CONTEXT NEWS\r\n    - Poland has started to build a large energy group following\r\nthe government's decision to shift the European Union's largest\r\ncoal miner into a state-controlled fund, Prime Minister Ewa\r\nKopacz said on Oct. 2.\r\n    - Kopacz told Gazeta Wyborcza newspaper: \"This is the start\r\nof building a large fuel-energy concern, which will be created\r\nby combining our power plants, energy groups and coal, which is\r\ntheir fuel.\"\r\n    - Her comments came a day after the state-controlled\r\nsupervisory board of publicly listed Tauron replaced the\r\nutility's chief executive with a new boss who has said he is\r\nready to continue talks to purchase a stricken coal mine the\r\nprevious management had resisted buying. The board also replaced\r\ntwo other executives, triggering two further resignations.\r\n    - Tauron investor relations:\r\n    http://bit.ly/1j7Shyd\r\n    http://bit.ly/1Lr9hf7\r\n    - Reuters: Polish utility Tauron's new CEO ready to renew\r\ntalks to buy coal mine [ID:nL5N1220NF]\r\n    - Reuters: Poland starting to build large coal-energy group\r\n-PM Kopacz [ID:nL5N1230AM]\r\n    \r\n    RELATED COLUMNS\r\n    Polish slippage [ID:nL3N1214EQ]\r\n    Law and injustice [ID:nL4N11732T]\r\n    Cuddling coal [ID:nL8N0ZI1FB]\r\n    \r\n    - For previous columns by the author, Reuters customers can\r\nclick on [ELLIOTT/]\r\n    (Editing by Rob Cox and Sarah Bailey)\r\n    ((dominic.elliott@thomsonreuters.com))\r\n    ((Reuters messaging:\r\ndominic.elliott.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))\r\n    (On Twitter https://twitter.com/DominicElliott)\r\n\r\n\r\nKeywords: POLAND COAL/TAURON POL ENERG BREAKINGVIEWS","headline":"BREAKINGVIEWS-Poland's coal mine meddling saps its credibility","date":"2015-10-05T08:50:33.343Z","tpc_list":["COM","BMAT","UTIL","MINE","ENER","MTAL","COAM","BACT","BOSS1","PRIV","PLCY","JOB","MNGISS","EMRG","PL","CEEU","EEU","BRV","VOTE","POL","CLM","COA","NRG","PWR","COAPWR","ELEU","OILI","BR","LEN","REP","CMPNY","MIN","OILG","MRG","DEAL1","MCE","AMERS","LATAM","EUROP","GEN","RTRS"],"instr_list":["TPE.WA","ENAE.WA","PETR4.SA"]},{"body":"    Oct 5 (Reuters) - Equus Mining Ltd <EQE.AX>:\r\n * Trading halt <EQE.AX>\r\n * Seeks trading halt pending announcement regarding a capital raising\r\n * Source text for Eikon [ID:nASX81YB8x]\r\n\r\n ((For more news, please click here [EQE.AX])) \r\n ((Bengaluru Newsroom;
